title="Elections in Northern Ireland">Elections</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x83/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">\xca\x83</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span> <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">shin-<span style="font-size:90%">FAYN</span></i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <small>Irish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Irish" title="Help:IPA/Irish">[\xca\x83\xc9\xaan\xca\xb2 \xcb\x88f\xca\xb2e\xcb\x90n\xca\xb2]</a></span>; English: <span lang="en">"Ourselves" or "We Ourselves"<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>)</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing</a><sup id="cite_ref-France24_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France24-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">Irish republican</a> political party active in both the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in are also the only party that may be elected to the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Westminster</a>.\n</p><p>The original Sinn F\xc3\xa9in organisation was founded in 1905 by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Griffith" title="Arthur Griffith">Arthur Griffith</a>. It took its current form in 1970 after a split within the party (with the other side becoming the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Ireland" title="Workers&#39; Party of Ireland">Workers\' Party of Ireland</a>) and has historically been associated with the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional Irish Republican Army</a> (IRA).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> has been <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Leader of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">party president</a> since February 2018.\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is the largest <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalist</a> party in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a>, and the joint-largest overall (alongside the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a>); it had four ministerial posts in the most recent <a href="/wiki/Consociationalism" title="Consociationalism">power-sharing</a> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a>. It holds seven of Northern Ireland\'s 18 seats\xe2\x80\x94the second-largest bloc after the Democratic Unionist Party (DUP)\xe2\x80\x94at <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Westminster</a>, where it follows a policy of <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionism</a>, refusing to attend parliament or vote on bills. It is the third-largest party, and the largest party on the left, in the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a>, the parliament of the Republic of Ireland.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Name"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Name</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#1905\xe2\x80\x931922"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">1905\xe2\x80\x931922</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#1923\xe2\x80\x931970"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">1923\xe2\x80\x931970</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#1970\xe2\x80\x931975"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">1970\xe2\x80\x931975</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#1976\xe2\x80\x931983"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">1976\xe2\x80\x931983</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#1983\xe2\x80\x931998"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">1983\xe2\x80\x931998</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#1998\xe2\x80\x932017"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">1998\xe2\x80\x932017</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#2018"><span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">2018</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Past_links_with_the_IRA"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Past links with the IRA</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Policy_and_ideology"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Policy and ideology</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Social_and_cultural"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Social and cultural</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#International_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">International relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#European_Union"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">European Union</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Organisational_structure"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Organisational structure</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Ard_Chomhairle_Officer_Board"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ard Chomhairle Officer Board</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Leadership_Members_elected_at_the_Ard_Fh\xc3\xa9is_2016"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Leadership Members elected at the Ard Fh\xc3\xa9is 2016</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Leadership_history"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Leadership history</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Ministers_and_spokespeople"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Ministers and spokespeople</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Northern_Ireland_Assembly"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Northern Ireland Assembly</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Seanad_\xc3\x89ireann"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#European_Parliament"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">European Parliament</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#General_election_results"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">General election results</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Northern_Ireland"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Northern Ireland</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28"><a href="#Devolved_legislature_elections"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Devolved legislature elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-29"><a href="#Westminster_elections"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Westminster elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-30"><a href="#Trends"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Trends</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann_elections"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Local_government_elections"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Local government elections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#European_elections"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">European elections</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The phrase "Sinn F\xc3\xa9in" is <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> for "Ourselves" or "We Ourselves",<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MacDonncha12_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonncha12-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> although it is frequently mistranslated as "ourselves alone" (from "<i>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Amh\xc3\xa1in</i>", an early 20th century slogan. See also <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_(slogan)" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in (slogan)">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in (slogan)</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The meaning of the name itself is an assertion of Irish national sovereignty and self-determination; i.e., the <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish people</a> governing themselves, rather than being part of a political union with Great Britain (England, Scotland and Wales) under the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Westminster Parliament</a>.\n</p><p>Around the time of 1969\xe2\x80\x931970, owing to the split in the republican movement, there were two groups calling themselves Sinn F\xc3\xa9in; one under <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Mac_Giolla" title="Tom\xc3\xa1s Mac Giolla">Tom\xc3\xa1s Mac Giolla</a>, the other under <a href="/wiki/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh" title="Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh">Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh</a>. The latter became known as Sinn F\xc3\xa9in (Kevin Street) or <b>Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</b>, and the former became known as Sinn F\xc3\xa9in (Gardiner Place) or Official Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. As the "Officials" dropped all mention of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in from their name in 1982, instead calling itself the Workers\' Party of Ireland, the Provisionals were now generally known as Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. Supporters of <a href="/wiki/Republican_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>, which came from a 1986 split, still use the term "Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in" to refer to the party led by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a>.\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members have also been referred to as Shinners, a term intended as a <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="History of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">History of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a></div>\n<h3><span id="1905.E2.80.931922"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1905\xe2\x80\x931922">1905\xe2\x80\x931922</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1905\xe2\x80\x931922">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Griffith_(1871-1922).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Arthur_Griffith_%281871-1922%29.jpg/220px-Arthur_Griffith_%281871-1922%29.jpg" width="220" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Arthur_Griffith_%281871-1922%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="314" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Griffith_(1871-1922).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arthur Griffith</div></div></div>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was founded on 28 November 1905, when, at the first annual Convention of the National Council, Arthur Griffith outlined the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in policy, "to establish in Ireland\'s capital a national legislature endowed with the moral authority of the Irish nation".<sup id="cite_ref-MacDonncha12_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonncha12-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The party contested the <a href="/wiki/North_Leitrim_by-election,_1908" title="North Leitrim by-election, 1908">1908 North Leitrim by-election</a>, where it secured 27% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Thereafter, both support and membership fell. At the 1910 <i>Ard Fheis</i> (party conference) the attendance was poor, and there was difficulty finding members willing to take seats on the executive.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg/220px-McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg/330px-McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGuinness-_1917_election.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The campaign car of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_McGuinness" title="Joseph McGuinness">Joseph McGuinness</a>, who won the 1917 <a href="/wiki/South_Longford_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="South Longford (UK Parliament constituency)">South Longford</a> by-election whilst imprisoned. He was one of the first Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members to be elected. In 1921 he sided with Collins in the Treaty debate.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1914, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members, including Griffith, joined the anti-Redmond <a href="/wiki/Irish_Volunteers" title="Irish Volunteers">Irish Volunteers</a>, which was referred to by <a href="/wiki/John_Redmond" title="John Redmond">Redmondites</a> and others as the "Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Volunteers". Although Griffith himself did not take part in the <a href="/wiki/Easter_Rising" title="Easter Rising">Easter Rising</a> of 1916, many Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members, who were also members of both the Volunteers and the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Brotherhood" title="Irish Republican Brotherhood">Irish Republican Brotherhood</a>, did. Government and newspapers dubbed the Rising "the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Rising".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> After the Rising, republicans came together under the banner of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, and at the 1917 <i>Ard Fheis</i> the party committed itself for the first time to the establishment of an <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1918" title="Irish general election, 1918">1918 general election</a>, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in won 73 of Ireland\'s 105 seats, and in January 1919, its MPs assembled in Dublin and proclaimed themselves <a href="/wiki/First_D%C3%A1il" title="First D\xc3\xa1il">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the parliament of Ireland. The party supported the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army_(1917%E2%80%9322)" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Republican Army (1917\xe2\x80\x9322)">Irish Republican Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">War of Independence</a>, and members of the D\xc3\xa1il government negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a> with the British government in 1921. In the D\xc3\xa1il debates that followed, the party divided on the Treaty. Anti-Treaty members led by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a> walked out, and pro- and anti-Treaty members took opposite sides in the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Irish_Civil_War" title="Irish Civil War">Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1923.E2.80.931970"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1923\xe2\x80\x931970">1923\xe2\x80\x931970</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1923\xe2\x80\x931970">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Pro-Treaty D\xc3\xa1il deputies and other Treaty supporters formed a new party, <a href="/wiki/Cumann_na_nGaedheal" title="Cumann na nGaedheal">Cumann na nGaedheal</a>, on 27 April 1923 at a meeting in Dublin, where delegates agreed on a constitution and political programme.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Cumann na nGaedheal went on to govern the new <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> for nine years. (It merged with two other organisations to form <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a> in 1933.)<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Anti-Treaty Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members continued to boycott the D\xc3\xa1il. At a special <i>Ard Fheis</i> in March 1926, de Valera proposed that elected members be allowed to take their seats in the D\xc3\xa1il if and when the controversial <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_Allegiance_(Ireland)" title="Oath of Allegiance (Ireland)">Oath of Allegiance</a> was removed. When his motion was defeated, de Valera resigned from Sinn F\xc3\xa9in; on 16 May 1926, he founded his own party, <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna F\xc3\xa1il">Fianna F\xc3\xa1il</a>, which was dedicated to republicanising the Free State from within its political structures. He took most Sinn F\xc3\xa9in TDs with him.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> De Valera\'s resignation meant also the loss of financial support from America.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The rump Sinn F\xc3\xa9in party could field no more than fifteen candidates,<sup id="cite_ref-Times270602_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times270602-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and won only six seats in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_June_1927" title="Irish general election, June 1927">June 1927 general election</a>, a level of support not seen since before 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Times270830_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times270830-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Vice-President and <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> leader <a href="/wiki/Mary_MacSwiney" title="Mary MacSwiney">Mary MacSwiney</a> announced that the party simply did not have the funds to contest <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_September_1927" title="Irish general election, September 1927">the second election called that year</a>, declaring "no true Irish citizen can vote for any of the other parties".<sup id="cite_ref-Times270830_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times270830-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Fianna F\xc3\xa1il came to power at the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1932" title="Irish general election, 1932">1932 general election</a> (to begin what would be an unbroken 16-year spell in government) and went on to long dominate politics in the independent Irish state.\n</p><p>An attempt in the 1940s to access funds that had been put in the care of the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_(Ireland)" title="High Court (Ireland)">High Court</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Funds_case" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Funds case">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Funds case</a>, which the party lost and in which the judge ruled that it was not the legal successor to the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in of 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1955" title="United Kingdom general election, 1955">United Kingdom 1955 general election</a>, two Sinn F\xc3\xa9in candidates were elected to Westminster, but the party\'s vote decreased at the following election in 1959, during the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army_(1922%E2%80%9369)" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Republican Army (1922\xe2\x80\x9369)">IRA</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Border_Campaign_(Irish_Republican_Army)" title="Border Campaign (Irish Republican Army)">Border Campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1962, supporters of <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism\xe2\x80\x93Leninism">Marxism\xe2\x80\x93Leninism</a> took control of the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in leadership from traditional republicans, and started to take policy in a new direction. The same thing happened in the IRA, with the ascent of <a href="/wiki/Cathal_Goulding" title="Cathal Goulding">Cathal Goulding</a>. These people were influenced by <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Ireland" title="Communist Party of Ireland">Communist Party of Ireland</a> member <a href="/wiki/Roy_Johnston" title="Roy Johnston">Roy Johnston</a>\'s "National Liberation Strategy" and the theories of <a href="/wiki/C._Desmond_Greaves" title="C. Desmond Greaves">C. Desmond Greaves</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Connolly_Association" title="Connolly Association">Connolly Association</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Great_Britain" title="Communist Party of Great Britain">Communist Party of Great Britain</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Garland" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Garland">Garland</a> Commission was set up in 1967, to investigate the possibility of ending abstentionism. Its report angered the already disaffected traditional republican element within the party, notably <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Mac_St%C3%ADof%C3%A1in" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Mac St\xc3\xadof\xc3\xa1in">Se\xc3\xa1n Mac St\xc3\xadof\xc3\xa1in</a> and Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh, who viewed such a policy as treason against the Irish Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1970.E2.80.931975"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1970\xe2\x80\x931975">1970\xe2\x80\x931975</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1970\xe2\x80\x931975">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg/220px-Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg/330px-Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg/440px-Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="542" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ruair%C3%AD_%C3%93_Br%C3%A1daigh" title="Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh">Ruair\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh</a> was the president of Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in from 1970 until 1983.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Sinn F\xc3\xa9in party split in two at the beginning of 1970. At the party\'s <i>Ard Fheis</i> on 11 January the proposal to end abstentionism and take seats, if elected, in the D\xc3\xa1il, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Parliament of Northern Ireland">Parliament of Northern Ireland</a> and the Parliament of the United Kingdom was put before the members.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> A similar motion had been adopted at an IRA convention the previous month, leading to the formation of a Provisional Army Council by Mac St\xc3\xadof\xc3\xa1in and other members opposed to the leadership. When the motion was put to the <i>Ard Fheis</i>, it failed to achieve the necessary two-thirds majority. The Executive attempted to circumvent this by introducing a motion in support of IRA policy, at which point the dissenting delegates walked out of the meeting. These members reconvened at another place, appointed a Caretaker Executive and pledged allegiance to the Provisional Army Council. The Caretaker Executive declared itself opposed to the ending of abstentionism, the drift towards "extreme forms of socialism", the failure of the leadership to defend the nationalist people of Belfast during the <a href="/wiki/1969_Northern_Ireland_riots" title="1969 Northern Ireland riots">1969 Northern Ireland riots</a>, and the expulsion of traditional republicans by the leadership during the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At its October 1970 <i>Ard Fheis</i>, delegates were informed that an IRA convention had been held and had regularised its structure, bringing to an end the \'provisional\' period.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> By then, however, the label "Provisional" or "Provo" was already being applied to them by the media.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The opposing, anti-abstentionist party became known as "Official Sinn F\xc3\xa9in".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It changed its name in 1977 to "Sinn F\xc3\xa9in \xe2\x80\x93 The Workers\' Party",<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and in 1982 to "<a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Ireland" title="Workers&#39; Party of Ireland">The Workers\' Party</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because the "Provisionals" were committed to military rather than political action, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s initial membership was largely confined, in <a href="/wiki/Danny_Morrison_(writer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Danny Morrison (writer)">Danny Morrison</a>\'s words, to men "over military age or women". A Sinn F\xc3\xa9in organiser of the time in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> described the party\'s role as "agitation and publicity".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> New <i>cumainn</i> (branches) were established in Belfast, and a new newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/Republican_News" title="Republican News">Republican News</a></i>, was published.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in took off as a protest movement after the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Demetrius" title="Operation Demetrius">internment</a> in August 1971, organising marches and pickets.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The party launched its platform, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire_Nua" title="\xc3\x89ire Nua">\xc3\x89ire Nua</a></i> ("a New Ireland") at the 1971 <i>Ard Fheis</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In general, however, the party lacked a distinct political philosophy. In the words of Brian Feeney, "\xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh would use Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <i>ard fheiseanna</i> (party conferences) to announce republican policy, which was, in effect, IRA policy, namely that Britain should leave the North or the \'war\' would continue".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was given a concrete presence in the community when the <a href="/wiki/Chronology_of_Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army_actions_(1970%E2%80%9379)#1975" title="Chronology of Provisional Irish Republican Army actions (1970\xe2\x80\x9379)">IRA declared a ceasefire in 1975</a>. \'Incident centres\' were set up to communicate potential confrontations to the British authorities. They were manned by Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, which had been legalised the previous year by <a href="/wiki/Merlyn_Rees" title="Merlyn Rees">Merlyn Rees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Secretary of State for Northern Ireland">Secretary of State for Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1976.E2.80.931983"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1976\xe2\x80\x931983">1976\xe2\x80\x931983</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1976\xe2\x80\x931983">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland@20160528_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg/220px-Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg/330px-Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg/440px-Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland%4020160528_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3113" data-file-height="2748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Sands_Belfast_Irland@20160528_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bobby_Sands" title="Bobby Sands">Bobby Sands</a> mural in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>. Sands, a member of the Provisional IRA, stood on an <a href="/wiki/Anti_H-Block" title="Anti H-Block">Anti H-Block</a> ticket.</div></div></div>\n<p>Political status for prisoners became an issue after the ending of the truce. Rees released the last of the internees but introduced the <a href="/wiki/Diplock_courts" title="Diplock courts">Diplock courts</a>, and ended \'<a href="/wiki/Special_Category_Status" title="Special Category Status">Special Category Status</a>\' for all prisoners convicted after 1 March 1976. This led first to the <a href="/wiki/Blanket_protest" title="Blanket protest">blanket protest</a>, and then to the <a href="/wiki/Dirty_protest" title="Dirty protest">dirty protest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Around the same time, Gerry Adams began writing for <i>Republican News</i>, calling for Sinn F\xc3\xa9in to become more involved politically.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Over the next few years, Adams and those aligned with him would extend their influence throughout the republican movement and slowly marginalise \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh, part of a general trend of power in both Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the IRA shifting north.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In particular, \xc3\x93\'Br\xc3\xa1daigh\'s part in the 1975 IRA ceasefire had damaged his reputation in the eyes of Ulster republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The prisoners\' protest climaxed with the <a href="/wiki/1981_Irish_hunger_strike" title="1981 Irish hunger strike">1981 hunger strike</a>, during which striker <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Sands" title="Bobby Sands">Bobby Sands</a> was elected Member of Parliament for <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh_and_South_Tyrone_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Fermanagh and South Tyrone (UK Parliament constituency)">Fermanagh and South Tyrone</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Anti_H-Block" title="Anti H-Block">Anti H-Block</a> candidate. After his death on hunger strike, his seat was held, with an increased vote, by his election agent, <a href="/wiki/Owen_Carron" title="Owen Carron">Owen Carron</a>. Two other Anti H-Block candidates were elected to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1981" title="Irish general election, 1981">general election in the Republic</a>. These successes convinced republicans that they should contest every election.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Danny Morrison expressed the mood at the 1981 <i>Ard Fheis</i> when he said:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>"Who here really believes we can win the war through the ballot box? But will anyone here object if, with a ballot paper in this hand and an Armalite in the other, we take power in Ireland?".<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_1997,_pp._281\xe2\x80\x932_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_1997,_pp._281\xe2\x80\x932-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p>This was the origin of what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Armalite_and_ballot_box_strategy" title="Armalite and ballot box strategy">Armalite and ballot box strategy</a>. <i>\xc3\x89ire Nua</i> was dropped in 1982, and the following year \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh stepped down as leader, and was replaced by Adams.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1983.E2.80.931998"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1983\xe2\x80\x931998">1983\xe2\x80\x931998</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1983\xe2\x80\x931998">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg/220px-Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg/330px-Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg/440px-Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerry_Adams_and_Martin_McGuinness.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Under the political leadership of Gerry Adams and <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a>, Provisional Sinn F\xc3\xa9in adopted a reformist policy, eventually leading to the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under Adams\' leadership electoral politics became increasingly important. In 1983 <a href="/wiki/Alex_Maskey" title="Alex Maskey">Alex Maskey</a> was elected to <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Council" title="Belfast City Council">Belfast City Council</a>, the first Sinn F\xc3\xa9in member to sit on that body.<sup id="cite_ref-murray_tonge153_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murray_tonge153-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in polled over 100,000 votes in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1983" title="United Kingdom general election, 1983">Westminster elections</a> that year, and Adams won the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">West Belfast</a> seat that had been held by the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> (SDLP).<sup id="cite_ref-murray_tonge153_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murray_tonge153-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> By <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_local_government_elections,_1985#Overall" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland local government elections, 1985">1985</a> it had fifty-nine seats on seventeen of the twenty-six Northern Ireland councils, including seven on Belfast City Council.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The party began a reappraisal of the policy of abstention from the D\xc3\xa1il. At the 1983 <i>Ard Fheis</i> the constitution was amended to remove the ban on the discussion of abstentionism to allow Sinn F\xc3\xa9in to run a candidate in the forthcoming European elections. However, in his address, Adams said, "We are an abstentionist party. It is not my intention to advocate change in this situation."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A motion to permit entry into the D\xc3\xa1il was allowed at the 1985 <i>Ard Fheis</i>, but without the active support of the leadership, and Adams did not speak. The motion failed narrowly.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> By October of the following year an IRA Convention had indicated its support for elected Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <a href="/wiki/Teachta%C3%AD_D%C3%A1la" class="mw-redirect" title="Teachta\xc3\xad D\xc3\xa1la">Teachta\xc3\xad D\xc3\xa1la</a> (TDs) taking their seats. Thus, when the motion to end abstention was put to the <i>Ard Fheis</i> on 1 November 1986, it was clear that there would not be a split in the IRA as there had been in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The motion was passed with a two-thirds majority. \xc3\x93 Br\xc3\xa1daigh and about twenty other delegates walked out, and met in a Dublin hotel with hundreds of supporters to re-organise as <a href="/wiki/Republican_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tentative negotiations between Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the British government led to more substantive discussions with the SDLP in the 1990s. Multi-party negotiations began in 1994 in Northern Ireland, without Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. The Provisional IRA declared a ceasefire in the autumn of 1994. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in then joined the talks, but the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> government under <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> soon came to depend on unionist votes to remain in power. It suspended Sinn F\xc3\xa9in from the talks, and began to insist that the IRA decommission all of their weapons before Sinn F\xc3\xa9in be re-admitted to the talks; this led to the IRA calling off its ceasefire. The new <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> wasn\'t reliant on unionist votes and re-admitted Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, leading to another, permanent, ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The talks led to the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> of 10 April 1998 (officially known as the <i>Belfast Agreement</i>), which set up an inclusive devolved government in the North, and altered the Dublin government\'s constitutional claim to the whole island in <a href="/wiki/Articles_2_and_3_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Articles 2 and 3 of the Constitution of Ireland">Articles 2 and 3 of the Constitution of Ireland</a>. Republicans opposed to the direction taken by Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in the peace process formed the <a href="/wiki/32_County_Sovereignty_Movement" title="32 County Sovereignty Movement">32 County Sovereignty Movement</a> in the late 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.932017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998\xe2\x80\x932017">1998\xe2\x80\x932017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1998\xe2\x80\x932017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The party expelled <a href="/wiki/Denis_Donaldson" title="Denis Donaldson">Denis Donaldson</a>, a party official, in December 2005, with him stating publicly that he had been in the employ of the British government as an agent since the 1980s. Donaldson told reporters that the British security agencies who employed him were behind the collapse of the Assembly and set up Sinn F\xc3\xa9in to take the blame for it, a claim disputed by the British Government.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Donaldson was found fatally shot in his home in <a href="/wiki/County_Donegal" title="County Donegal">County Donegal</a> on 4 April 2006, and a murder inquiry was launched.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In April 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Real_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Real Irish Republican Army">Real IRA</a> released a statement taking responsibility for the killing.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg/170px-Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg.png" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg/255px-Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg/340px-Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="316" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alternative logo \xe2\x80\x93 glyph version</div></div></div>\n<p>When Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the Democratic Unionist Party (DUP) became the largest parties, by the terms of the Good Friday Agreement no deal could be made without the support of both parties. They nearly reached a deal in November 2004, but the DUP insisted on photographic and/or video evidence that decommissioning had been carried out, which was unacceptable to Sinn F\xc3\xa9in.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 September 2006, Martin McGuinness publicly stated that Sinn F\xc3\xa9in would refuse to participate in a shadow assembly at Stormont, asserting that his party would only take part in negotiations that were aimed at restoring a power-sharing government. This development followed a decision on the part of members of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in to refrain from participating in debates since the Assembly\'s recall the previous May. The relevant parties to these talks were given a deadline of 24 November 2006 to decide upon whether or not they would ultimately form the executive.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 86-year Sinn F\xc3\xa9in boycott of policing in Northern Ireland ended on 28 January 2007, when the <i>Ard Fheis</i> voted overwhelmingly to support the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">Police Service of Northern Ireland</a> (PSNI).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members began to sit on Policing Boards and join District Policing Partnerships.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> There was opposition to this decision within Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, and some members left, including elected representatives. The most well-known opponent was former IRA prisoner <a href="/wiki/Gerry_McGeough" title="Gerry McGeough">Gerry McGeough</a>, who stood in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election,_2007" title="Northern Ireland Assembly election, 2007">2007 Assembly election</a> against Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh_and_South_Tyrone_(Assembly_constituency)" title="Fermanagh and South Tyrone (Assembly constituency)">Fermanagh and South Tyrone</a>, as an Independent Republican.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Others who opposed this development left to found the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Network_for_Unity" title="Republican Network for Unity">Republican Network for Unity</a>.\n</p><p>Immediately after the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">June 2017 UK general election</a>, where the Conservatives won 49% of seats but not an overall majority, so that non-mainstream parties could have significant influence, Gerry Adams announced for Sinn F\xc3\xa9in that their elected MPs would continue the policy of not swearing <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_Allegiance_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oath of Allegiance (UK)">allegiance to the Queen</a>, as would be required for them to take their seats in the Westminster Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 and 2018 there were allegations of bullying within the party, leading to a number of resignations and expulsions of elected members.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the <i>Ard Fheis</i> on 18 November 2017, Gerry Adams announced he would stand down as president of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in 2018, and would not stand for re-election as <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TD</a> for <a href="/wiki/Louth_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Louth (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Louth</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg/220px-Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg/330px-Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg/440px-Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3182" data-file-height="2074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Lou_McDonald_and_Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mary Lou McDonald and Michelle O\xe2\x80\x99Neill</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 10 February 2018, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> was announced as the new president of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in at a special Ard Fheis in Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-Lou_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lou-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michelle_O%E2%80%99Neill" class="mw-redirect" title="Michelle O\xe2\x80\x99Neill">Michelle O\xe2\x80\x99Neill</a> was also elected as Vice President of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-Lou_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lou-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> McDonald has made clear that as President of Sinn Fein, her ambition is to be in government north and south - and is willing to work in coalition as the major or minor party of government in the southern jurisdiction, a shift in policy compared to Adams ambition to govern as a minority government in the Oireachtas.\n</p><p>Sinn Fein have been a leading opponent of Northern Ireland <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">leaving the European Union</a> together with the rest of the United Kingdom, with <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a> suggesting a referendum on the <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">reunification of Ireland</a> immediately after the <a href="/wiki/UK_EU_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="UK EU referendum">UK EU referendum</a> results were announced,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> a stance later reiterated by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> as a way of resolving the <a href="/wiki/Irish_border_question" title="Irish border question">Irish border question</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-France24_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France24-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_links_with_the_IRA">Past links with the IRA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Past links with the IRA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is the largest <a href="/wiki/Irish_republican" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish republican">Irish republican</a> political party, and was historically associated with the IRA, while also having been associated with the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional IRA">Provisional IRA</a> in the party\xc2\xb4s modern incarnation. The Irish government alleged that senior members of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in have held posts on the <a href="/wiki/IRA_Army_Council" title="IRA Army Council">IRA Army Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> However, the SF leadership has denied these claims.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The US Government has made similar allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A republican document of the early 1980s stated: "Both Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the IRA play different but converging roles in the war of national liberation. The Irish Republican Army wages an armed campaign... Sinn F\xc3\xa9in maintains the propaganda war and is the public and political voice of the movement".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">British government</a> stated in 2005 that "we had always said all the way through we believed that Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the IRA were inextricably linked and that had obvious implications at leadership level".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Bank_robbery" title="Northern Bank robbery">Northern Bank robbery</a> of \xc2\xa326.5 million in Belfast in December 2004 further delayed a political deal in Northern Ireland. The IRA were widely blamed for the robbery<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> although Sinn F\xc3\xa9in denied this and stated that party officials had not known of the robbery nor sanctioned it.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Because of the timing of the robbery, it is considered that the plans for the robbery must have been laid whilst Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was engaged in talks about a possible peace settlement. This undermined confidence among <a href="/wiki/Unionism_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unionism (Ireland)">unionists</a> about the sincerity of republicans towards reaching agreement. In the aftermath of the row over the robbery, a further controversy erupted when, on <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann">RT\xc3\x89</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Questions_and_Answers_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Questions and Answers (TV series)">Questions and Answers</a></i> programme, the chairman of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, <a href="/wiki/Mitchel_McLaughlin" title="Mitchel McLaughlin">Mitchel McLaughlin</a>, insisted that the IRA\'s controversial killing of a mother of ten young children, <a href="/wiki/Jean_McConville" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean McConville">Jean McConville</a>, in the early 1970s though "wrong", was not a crime, as it had taken place in the context of the political conflict. Politicians from the Republic, along with the Irish media, strongly attacked McLaughlin\'s comments.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 February 2005, the government-appointed <a href="/wiki/Independent_Monitoring_Commission" title="Independent Monitoring Commission">Independent Monitoring Commission</a> reported that it firmly supported the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">PSNI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na</a> assessments that the IRA was responsible for the Northern Bank robbery and that certain senior members of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in were also senior members of the IRA and would have had knowledge of and given approval to the carrying out of the robbery.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in has argued that the IMC is not independent, and that the inclusion of former <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/John_Alderdice" class="mw-redirect" title="John Alderdice">John Alderdice</a> and a British security head was proof of this.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The IMC recommended further financial sanctions against Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members of the Northern Ireland Assembly. The British government responded by saying it would ask MPs to vote to withdraw the parliamentary allowances of the four Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MPs elected in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gerry Adams responded to the IMC report by challenging the Irish government to have him arrested for IRA membership\xe2\x80\x94a crime in both jurisdictions\xe2\x80\x94and for <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspiracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 February 2005, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Justice_and_Equality" title="Minister for Justice and Equality">Irish Minister for Justice, Equality and Law Reform</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_McDowell_(politician)" title="Michael McDowell (politician)">Michael McDowell</a> publicly accused three of the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in leadership, Gerry Adams, <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Ferris" title="Martin Ferris">Martin Ferris</a> (TD for <a href="/wiki/Kerry_North_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Kerry North (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Kerry North</a>) of being on the seven-man <a href="/wiki/IRA_Army_Council" title="IRA Army Council">IRA Army Council</a>; they later denied this.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 February 2005, a demonstration against the murder of <a href="/wiki/Robert_McCartney_(murder_victim)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert McCartney (murder victim)">Robert McCartney</a> on 30 January 2005 was held in east Belfast. <a href="/wiki/Alex_Maskey" title="Alex Maskey">Alex Maskey</a>, a former Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of Belfast">Lord Mayor of Belfast</a>, was told by relatives of McCartney to "hand over the 12" IRA members involved.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The McCartney family, although formerly Sinn F\xc3\xa9in voters themselves, urged witnesses to the crime to contact the PSNI.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Three IRA men were expelled from the organisation, and a man was charged with McCartney\'s murder.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Irish <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> <a href="/wiki/Bertie_Ahern" title="Bertie Ahern">Bertie Ahern</a> subsequently called Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the IRA "both sides of the same coin".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The official ostracism of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was shown in February 2005 when <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> passed a motion condemning the party\'s alleged involvement in illegal activity. US President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Edward Kennedy</a> refused to meet Gerry Adams while meeting the family of Robert McCartney.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 March 2005, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> in London passed without significant opposition a motion, introduced by the British government, to withdraw the allowances of the four Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MPs for one year, in response to the Northern Bank Robbery. This measure cost the party approximately \xc2\xa3400,000. However, the debate prior to the vote mainly surrounded the more recent events connected with the murder of Robert McCartney. Conservatives and unionists put down amendments to have the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MPs evicted from their offices at the House of Commons but these were defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2005, <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Reiss" title="Mitchell Reiss">Mitchell Reiss</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Special_Envoy_for_Northern_Ireland" title="United States Special Envoy for Northern Ireland">United States Special Envoy for Northern Ireland</a>, condemned the party\'s links to the IRA, saying "it is hard to understand how a European country in the year 2005 can have a private army associated with a political party".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The October 2015 <a href="/wiki/Assessment_on_Paramilitary_Groups_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Assessment on Paramilitary Groups in Northern Ireland">Assessment on Paramilitary Groups in Northern Ireland</a> concluded that the Provisional IRA still existed "in a much reduced form", and that some IRA members believed its Army Council oversaw both the PIRA and Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, although it believed that the leadership "remains committed to the peace process and its aim of achieving a united Ireland by political means".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_and_ideology">Policy and ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Policy and ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Fein_sign,_Strabane,_January_2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG/220px-Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG/330px-Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG/440px-Sinn_Fein_sign%2C_Strabane%2C_January_2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Fein_sign,_Strabane,_January_2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Republican_Youth" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Republican Youth">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Republican Youth</a> signs in <a href="/wiki/Strabane" title="Strabane">Strabane</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the party\'s policies are intended to be implemented on an "all-Ireland" basis which further emphasises their central aim of creating a <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">united Ireland</a>.\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic socialist">democratic socialist</a> and left-wing party.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, the party aligns itself with the <a href="/wiki/European_United_Left%E2%80%93Nordic_Green_Left" title="European United Left\xe2\x80\x93Nordic Green Left">European United Left\xe2\x80\x93Nordic Green Left</a> (GUE/NGL) parliamentary group. The party pledges support for minority rights, migrants\' rights, and eradicating poverty. Although it is not in favour of the extension of legalised abortion (British 1967 Act) to Northern Ireland, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in state they are opposed to the attitudes in society which "pressurise women" to have abortions and "criminalise" women who make this decision. The party does state that in cases of incest, rape, sexual abuse, "fatal foetal abnormalities", or when a woman\'s life and health are at risk or in danger, the final decision must rest with the woman.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Abortion_Referendum_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Abortion Referendum 2018">2018 Irish abortion referendum</a>, the party campaigned for a \'Yes\' vote, but remained opposed to abortions up to 12 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Categorised as "populist socialist" in literature,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> in 2014 leading party strategist and ideologue <a href="/wiki/Eoin_%C3%93_Broin" title="Eoin \xc3\x93 Broin">Eoin \xc3\x93 Broin</a> described Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s entire political project as unashamedly populist.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in has been considered to be <a href="/wiki/Eurosceptic" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurosceptic">Eurosceptic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The party campaigned for a "No" vote in the Irish <a href="/wiki/Third_Amendment_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Third Amendment of the Constitution of Ireland">referendum</a> on joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in was on the same side of the debate as the DUP and most of the UUP in that they wanted to pull out when UK had its referendum in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The party was critical of the supposed need for an <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">EU constitution</a> as proposed in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes2005_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes2005-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and urged a "No" vote in the 2008 referendum on the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a>, although Mary Lou McDonald said that there was "no contradiction in being pro-Europe, but anti-treaty".<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In its manifesto for the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 UK general election</a>, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in pledged that the party would campaign for the UK to stay within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), Martin McGuinness saying that an exit "would be absolutely economically disastrous". Gerry Adams said that, if there were to be a referendum on the question, there ought to be a separate and binding referendum for Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Irish_Times_EU_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irish_Times_EU-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Its policy of a "Europe of Equals", and its critical engagement after 2001, together with its engagement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, marks a change from the party\'s previous opposition to the EU. The party expresses, on one hand, "support for Europe-wide measures that promote and enhance human rights, equality and <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">the all-Ireland agenda</a>", and on the other a "principled opposition" to a <a href="/wiki/European_superstate" class="mw-redirect" title="European superstate">European superstate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bean2008_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bean2008-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_cultural">Social and cultural</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Social and cultural">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s main political goal is a <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">united Ireland</a>. Other key policies from their most recent election manifesto are listed below:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The 18 <a href="/wiki/List_of_MPs_for_Northern_Irish_constituencies_2010-" class="mw-redirect" title="List of MPs for Northern Irish constituencies 2010-">Northern Ireland MPs</a> who sit or have sat in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a> to be allowed to sit in D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann as full Deputies as well<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Ending academic selection within the education system<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Support for a "Minister for Children"</li>\n<li>Diplomatic pressure to close <a href="/wiki/Sellafield" title="Sellafield">Sellafield</a> nuclear reprocessing plant (in Britain)</li>\n<li>A draft Irish Language Bill for Northern Ireland (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acht_na_Gaeilge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Acht na Gaeilge (page does not exist)">Acht na Gaeilge</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> a Bill that would give the Irish Language the same status that the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> has in Wales</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Plastic_bag_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Plastic bag tax">Plastic bag levy</a>" to be extended to Northern Ireland</li>\n<li>To further <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> teaching in Northern Ireland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">Same-sex marriage</a> to be extended to Northern Ireland<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Increase in <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deposit_interest_retention_tax" title="Deposit interest retention tax">deposit interest retention tax</a></li>\n<li>A cap on public sector pay at three times the <a href="/wiki/Average_worker%27s_wage" title="Average worker&#39;s wage">average worker\'s wage</a></li>\n<li>A cap on the salaries of TDs and government ministers</li>\n<li>Standardisation of discretionary tax reliefs</li>\n<li>Greater state investment in the economy</li>\n<li>Reducing mortgage interest tax relief for landlords and property-based tax reliefs</li>\n<li>Establishment of a government fund to aid small and medium enterprises</li>\n<li>An "all-Ireland" economy with a common currency and one tax policy</li>\n<li>Greater investment for those who are <a href="/wiki/Disabled" class="mw-redirect" title="Disabled">disabled</a><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>An "All-Ireland-Health-Service" akin to the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> of the United Kingdom</li>\n<li>Cap on consultants\' pay</li>\n<li>Abolishment of prescription charges for medical card patients</li>\n<li>Expansion of primary care centres</li>\n<li>Gradual removal of subsidies of private practice in public hospitals and the introduction of a charge for practitioners for the use of public equipment and staff in their private practice</li>\n<li>Free breast screening (to check for breast cancer) of all women over forty<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in supports the creation of a "Minister for Europe", the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a> from Spain and France,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian conflict">Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in support a policy of "critical engagement with the EU", and have a "principled opposition" to a <a href="/wiki/European_superstate" class="mw-redirect" title="European superstate">European superstate</a>. It opposes an <a href="/wiki/EU_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="EU constitution">EU constitution</a> because it would reduce the <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> of the member-states.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> It also criticises the EU on grounds of <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a>. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Carthy" title="Matt Carthy">Matt Carthy</a> says that the "European Union must become a cooperative union of nation states committed to working together on issues such as climate change, migration, trade, and using our common strengths to improve the lives of citizens. If it does not, EU disintegration becomes a real possibility."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The party did however support continued UK membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">2016 EU referendum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisational_structure">Organisational structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Organisational structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39"
