srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(November 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_elected_representatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in elected representatives">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in elected representatives</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre,_Castlewellan,_December_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG/180px-Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG" width="180" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG/270px-Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG/360px-Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre%2C_Castlewellan%2C_December_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Fein_Advice_Centre,_Castlewellan,_December_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Sinn F\xc3\xa9in advice centre in <a href="/wiki/Castlewellan" title="Castlewellan">Castlewellan</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is organised throughout Ireland, and membership is open to all Irish residents over the age of 16. The party is organised hierarchically into <i><a href="/wiki/Cumainn" class="mw-redirect" title="Cumainn">cumainn</a></i> (branches), <i>comhairle ceantair</i> (district executives), and <i>c\xc3\xbaig\xc3\xad</i> (regional executives). At national level, the <i>Coiste Seasta</i> (Standing Committee) oversees the day-to-day running of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. It is an eight-member body nominated by the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <i><a href="/wiki/Ard_Chomhairle" class="mw-redirect" title="Ard Chomhairle">Ard Chomhairle</a></i> (National Executive) and also includes the chairperson of each <i>c\xc3\xbaige</i>. The Sinn F\xc3\xa9in <i>Ard Chomhairle</i> meets at least once a month. It directs the overall implementation of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in policy and activities of the party.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Ard Chomhairle</i> also oversees the operation of various departments of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in, viz Administration, Finance, National Organiser, Campaigns, <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Republican_Youth" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Republican Youth">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Republican Youth</a>, Women\'s Forum, Culture, Publicity and International Affairs. It is made up of the following: Officer Board and nine other members, all of whom are elected by delegates to the <i>Ard Fheis</i>, fifteen representing the five <i>C\xc3\xbaige</i> regions (three delegates each). The <i>Ard Chomhairle</i> can co-opt eight members for specific posts and additional members can be co-opted, if necessary, to ensure that at least thirty per cent of <i>Ard Chomhairle</i> members are women.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ardfheis" title="Ardfheis">Ardfheis</a> (national delegate conference) is the ultimate policy-making body of the party, where delegates, directly elected by members of <i>cumainn</i>, can decide on and implement policy. It is held at least once a year, but a special <i>Ard Fheis</i> can be called by the <i>Ard Chomhairle</i> or the membership under special circumstances.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ard_Chomhairle_Officer_Board">Ard Chomhairle Officer Board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ard Chomhairle Officer Board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>2016\xe2\x80\x932017<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>President: Gerry Adams</li>\n<li>Vice-President: <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a></li>\n<li>Chairperson: <a href="/wiki/Declan_Kearney" title="Declan Kearney">Declan when a new executive is formed. Other ministerial positions will not be allocated until then.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="D.C3.A1il_.C3.89ireann"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dd><i>See also:</i> <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in_Front_Bench" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in Front data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />6th\n</td>\n<td>238,915\n</td>\n<td>29.4%\n</td>\n<td>0.7%\n</td>\n<td style="background:#c5d2ea;">Abstention\n</td>\n<td>Gerry Adams\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trends">Trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in returned to Northern Ireland elections at the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election,_1982" title="Northern Ireland Assembly election, 1982">1982 Assembly elections</a>, winning five seats with 64,191 votes (10.1%). The party narrowly missed winning additional seats in <a href="/wiki/Belfast_North_(Assembly_constituency)" title="Belfast North (Assembly constituency)">Belfast North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh_and_South_Tyrone_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Fermanagh and South Tyrone (UK Parliament constituency)">Fermanagh and South Tyrone</a>. In the 1983 UK general election eight months later, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in increased its support, breaking the six-figure vote barrier in Northern Ireland for the first time by polling 102,701 votes (13.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Gerry Adams won the Belfast West constituency, and Danny Morrison fell only 78 votes short of victory in <a href="/wiki/Mid_Ulster_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Mid Ulster (UK Parliament constituency)">Mid Ulster</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1984_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1984 (United Kingdom)">1984 European elections</a> proved to be a disappointment, with Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s candidate Danny Morrison polling 91,476 (13.3%) and falling well behind the SDLP candidate <a href="/wiki/John_Hume" title="John Hume">John Hume</a>.\n</p><p>By the beginning of 1985, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in had won its first representation on local councils, owing to three by-election wins in Omagh (Seamus Kerr, May 1983) and Belfast (Alex Maskey in June 1983 and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Area_F#1984_by-election" title="Belfast Area F">Sean McKnight in March 1984</a>). Three sitting councillors also defected to Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in Dungannon, Fermanagh and Derry (the last defecting from the SDLP).<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1985_local_election_results_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1985_local_election_results-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Sinn F\xc3\xa9in succeeded in winning 59 seats in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_local_elections,_1985" title="Northern Ireland local elections, 1985">1985 local government elections</a>, after it had predicted winning only 40 seats. However, the results continued to show a decline from the peak of 1983, as the party won 75,686 votes (11.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-1985_local_election_results_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1985_local_election_results-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The party failed to gain any seats in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_by-elections,_1986" title="Northern Ireland by-elections, 1986">1986 by-elections</a> caused by the resignation of unionist MPs in protest at the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Agreement" title="Anglo-Irish Agreement">Anglo-Irish Agreement</a>. While this was partly due to an electoral pact between unionist candidates, the SF vote fell in the four constituencies they contested.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1987" title="United Kingdom general election, 1987">1987 general election</a>, Gerry Adams held his Belfast West seat, but the party failed to make breakthroughs elsewhere and overall polled 83,389 votes (11.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The same year saw the party contest the D\xc3\xa1il election in the Republic of Ireland; however, it failed to win any seats and polled less than 2%.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_local_elections,_1989" title="Northern Ireland local elections, 1989">1989 local government elections</a> saw a drop in support for Sinn F\xc3\xa9in.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Defending 58 seats (the 59 won in 1985, plus two 1987 by-election gains in West Belfast, minus three councillors who had defected to Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in 1986), the party lost 15 seats. In the aftermath of the election, Mitchell McLaughlin admitted that recent IRA activity had affected the Sinn F\xc3\xa9in vote.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1989_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 1989 (United Kingdom)">1989 European election</a>, Danny Morrison again failed to win a seat, polling at 48,914 votes (9%).\n</p><p>The nadir for SF in this period came in 1992, with Gerry Adams losing his Belfast West seat to the SDLP, and the SF vote falling in the other constituencies that they had contested relative to 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1997" title="United Kingdom general election, 1997">1997 UK general election</a>, Adams regained Belfast West. <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a> also won a seat in <a href="/wiki/Mid_Ulster_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Mid Ulster (UK Parliament constituency)">Mid Ulster</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1997" title="Irish general election, 1997">Irish general election the same year</a> the party won its first seat since <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1957" title="Irish general election, 1957">1957</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Caoimhgh%C3%ADn_%C3%93_Caol%C3%A1in" title="Caoimhgh\xc3\xadn \xc3\x93 Caol\xc3\xa1in">Caoimhgh\xc3\xadn \xc3\x93 Caol\xc3\xa1in</a> gaining a seat in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cavan-Monaghan_(Dail_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cavan-Monaghan (Dail constituency) (page does not exist)">Cavan-Monaghan constituency</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_1999" title="Irish local elections, 1999">Irish local elections of 1999</a> the party increased its number of councillors from 7 to 23.\n</p><p>The party overtook its nationalist rival, the Social Democratic and Labour Party, as the largest nationalist party in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_local_elections,_2001" title="Northern Ireland local elections, 2001">local elections</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2001_(Northern_Ireland)" title="United Kingdom general election, 2001 (Northern Ireland)">UK general election</a> of 2001, winning four Westminster seats to the SDLP\'s three.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The party continues to subscribe, however, to an <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionist</a> policy towards the Westminster British parliament, on account of opposing that parliament\'s jurisdiction in Northern Ireland, as well as its oath to the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg" class="image" title="Results in Northern Ireland from UK General Elections. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in increased its number of seats from two in 1997 to five in 2005, four of them in the west. It retained its five seats in 2010, was reduced to four in 2015 before increasing to seven in 2017."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg/1000px-Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg.png" width="1000" height="507" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg/1500px-Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg/2000px-Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="710" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Ireland_election_seats_1997-2017.svg" title="File:Northern Ireland election seats 1997-2017.svg"> </a></div>Results in Northern Ireland from UK General Elections. Sinn F\xc3\xa9in increased its number of seats from two in 1997 to five in 2005, four of them in the west. It retained its five seats in 2010, was reduced to four in 2015 before increasing to seven in 2017.</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in increased its share of the nationalist vote in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_Election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Assembly Election, 2003">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_Election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Assembly Election, 2007">2007</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_Election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Assembly Election, 2011">2011 Assembly elections</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Martin_McGuinness" title="Martin McGuinness">Martin McGuinness</a>, former Minister for Education, taking the post of <a href="/wiki/Deputy_First_Minister_of_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputy First Minister of Northern Ireland">deputy First Minister</a> in the Northern Ireland power-sharing Executive Committee. The party has three ministers in the Executive Committee.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 General Election</a>, the party retained its five seats,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCE_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCE-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and for the first time topped the poll at a Westminster Election in Northern Ireland, winning 25.5% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-ARK_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARK-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> All Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MPs increased their share of the vote and with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Fermanagh_and_South_Tyrone_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Fermanagh and South Tyrone (UK Parliament constituency)">Fermanagh and South Tyrone</a>, increased their majorities.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCE_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCE-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In Fermanagh and South Tyrone, <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionism#Unionism_in_Northern_Ireland_today" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster Unionism">Unionist</a> parties agreed a joint candidate,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> this resulted in the closest contest of the election, with Sinn F\xc3\xa9in MP <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Gildernew" title="Michelle Gildernew">Michelle Gildernew</a> holding her seat by 4 votes after 3 recounts and an election petition challenging the result.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in lost some ground in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election,_2016" title="Northern Ireland Assembly election, 2016">2016 Assembly election</a>, dropping one seat to finish with 28, ten behind the DUP.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election,_2017" title="Northern Ireland Assembly election, 2017">snap election</a> eight months later caused by the resignation of McGuinness as deputy First Minister, however, the party surged, winning 27.9% of the popular vote to 28.1% for the DUP, and 27 seats to the DUP\'s 28 in an Assembly reduced by 18 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The withdrawal of the DUP party whip from <a href="/wiki/Jim_Wells_(politician)" title="Jim Wells (politician)">Jim Wells</a> in May 2018 meant that Sinn F\xc3\xa9in became the joint-largest party in the Assembly alongside the DUP, with 27 seats each.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="D.C3.A1il_.C3.89ireann_elections"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann_elections">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 15%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />9\n</td>\n<td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />3rd\n</td>\n<td>295,319\n</td>\n<td>13.8%\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fcc;">Opposition\n</td>\n<td>Gerry Adams\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The party had five TDs elected in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2002" title="Irish general election, 2002">2002 Irish general election</a>, an increase of four from the previous election. At the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2007" title="Irish general election, 2007">general election in 2007</a> the party had expectations of substantial gains,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> with poll predictions that they would gain five<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> to ten seats.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> However, the party lost one of its seats to <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a>. <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Crowe" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Crowe">Se\xc3\xa1n Crowe</a>, who had topped the poll in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_South%E2%80%93West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dublin South\xe2\x80\x93West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency) (page does not exist)">Dublin South\xe2\x80\x93West</a> fell to fifth place, with his first preference vote reduced from 20.28% to 12.16%.<sup id="cite_ref-2007results_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007results-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 November 2010, <a href="/wiki/Pearse_Doherty" title="Pearse Doherty">Pearse Doherty</a> won a seat in the <a href="/wiki/Donegal_South%E2%80%93West_by-election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Donegal South\xe2\x80\x93West by-election, 2010">Donegal South\xe2\x80\x93West by-election</a>. It was the party\'s first by-election victory in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> since 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> After negotiations with the left-wing Independent TDs <a href="/wiki/Finian_McGrath" title="Finian McGrath">Finian McGrath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maureen_O%27Sullivan_(politician)" title="Maureen O&#39;Sullivan (politician)">Maureen O\'Sullivan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Technical_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical Group">Technical Group</a> was formed in the D\xc3\xa1il to give its members more speaking time.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2011" title="Irish general election, 2011">2011 Irish general election</a> the party made significant gains. All its sitting TDs were returned, with Se\xc3\xa1n Crowe regaining the seat he had lost in 2007 in Dublin South\xe2\x80\x93West. In addition to winning long-targeted seats such as <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Central_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Dublin Central (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Dublin Central</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_North%E2%80%93West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dublin North\xe2\x80\x93West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency) (page does not exist)">Dublin North\xe2\x80\x93West</a>, the party gained unexpected seats in <a href="/wiki/Cork_East_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Cork East (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Cork East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sligo%E2%80%93North_Leitrim_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Sligo\xe2\x80\x93North Leitrim (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Sligo\xe2\x80\x93North Leitrim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IT1_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IT1-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> It ultimately won 14 seats, the best performance for the party\'s current incarnation. The party went on to win three seats in the Seanad election which followed their success at the general election.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2016" title="Irish general election, 2016">2016 election</a> it made further gains, finishing with 23 seats and overtaking the Labour Party as the third-largest party in the D\xc3\xa1il.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> It ran seven candidates in the Seanad election, all of whom were successful.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government_elections">Local government elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Local government elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Election\n</th>\n<th>Country\n</th>\n<th>First preference vote\n</th>\n<th>Vote&#160;%\n</th>\n<th>Seats\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_1920" title="Irish local elections, 1920">1920</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">Ireland\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="center">27.0%\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_1974" title="Irish local elections, 1974">1974</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="left"><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">7 / 802</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 23%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_2014" title="Irish local elections, 2014">2014</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">Republic of Ireland\n</td>\n<td align="center">258,650\n</td>\n<td align="center">15.2%\n</td>\n<td align="left"><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">159 / 949</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 17%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in is represented on most county and city councils. It made large gains in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_2004" title="Irish local elections, 2004">local elections of 2004</a>, increasing its number of councillors from 21 to 54, and replacing the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democrats" title="Progressive Democrats">Progressive Democrats</a> as the fourth-largest party in local government.<sup id="cite_ref-results2004_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-results2004-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Irish_local_elections,_2009" title="Irish local elections, 2009">local elections of June 2009</a>, the party\'s vote fell by 0.95% to 7.34%, with no change in the number of seats. Losses in Dublin and urban areas were balanced by gains in areas such as Limerick, Wicklow, Cork, Tipperary and Kilkenny and the border counties .<sup id="cite_ref-2009results_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009results-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> However, three of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s seven representatives on <a href="/wiki/Dublin_City_Council" title="Dublin City Council">Dublin City Council</a> resigned within six months of the June 2009 elections, one of them defecting to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_elections">European elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinn_F%C3%A9in&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: European elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Election\n</th>\n<th>Country\n</th>\n<th>First preference vote\n</th>\n<th>Vote&#160;%\n</th>\n<th>Seats\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;" rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1984" title="European Parliament election, 1984">1984</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1984_(United_Kingdom)#Northern_Ireland" title="European Parliament election, 1984 (United Kingdom)">Northern Ireland</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">91,476\n</td>\n<td align="center">13.3%\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">0 / 3</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 0%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;" rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014" title="European Parliament election, 2014">2014</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">Northern Ireland</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">159,813\n</td>\n<td align="center">25.5%\n</td>\n<td align="left"><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">1 / 3</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 33%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(Ireland)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (Ireland)">Republic of Ireland</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">323,300\n</td>\n<td align="center">19.5%\n</td>\n<td align="left"><div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">3 / 11</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #008800; width: 27%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004" title="European Parliament election, 2004">2004 European Parliament election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bairbre_de_Br%C3%BAn" title="Bairbre de Br\xc3\xban">Bairbre de Br\xc3\xban</a> won Sinn F\xc3\xa9in\'s first seat in the European Parliament, at the expense of the Social Democratic and Labour Party (SDLP). She came in second behind <a href="/wiki/Jim_Allister" title="Jim Allister">Jim Allister</a>, then of the Democratic Unionist Party (DUP).<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009" title="European Parliament election, 2009">2009 election</a>, de Br\xc3\xban was re-elected with 126,184 first preference votes, the only candidate to reach the quota on the first count. This was the first time since elections began in 1979 that the DUP failed to take the first seat, and was the first occasion Sinn F\xc3\xa9in topped a poll in any Northern Ireland election.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sinn F\xc3\xa9in made a breakthrough in the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Dublin (European Parliament constituency)">Dublin constituency</a> in <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004_(Ireland)" title="European Parliament election, 2004 (Ireland)">2004</a>. The party\'s candidate, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a>, was elected on the sixth count as one of four MEPs for Dublin, effectively taking the seat of <a href="/wiki/Patricia_McKenna" title="Patricia McKenna">Patricia McKenna</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(Ireland)" title="Green Party (Ireland)">Green Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2009_(Ireland)" title="European Parliament election, 2009 (Ireland)">2009 election</a>, when Dublin\'s representation was reduced to three MEPs, she failed to hold her seat.<sup id="cite_ref-Election_Ireland_results_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Election_Ireland_results-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In the South constituency their candidate, Councillor <a href="/wiki/Toir%C3%A9asa_Ferris" title="Toir\xc3\xa9asa Ferris">Toir\xc3\xa9asa Ferris</a>, managed to nearly double the number of first preference votes,<sup id="cite_ref-Election_Ireland_results_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Election_Ireland_results-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> lying third after the first count, but failed to get enough transfers to win a seat.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014" title="European Parliament election, 2014">2014 election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martina_Anderson" title="Martina Anderson">Martina Anderson</a> topped the poll in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Northern Ireland (European Parliament constituency)">Northern Ireland</a>, as did <a href="/wiki/Lynn_Boylan" title="Lynn Boylan">Lynn Boylan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Dublin (European Parliament constituency)">Dublin</a>. <a href="/wiki/Liadh_N%C3%AD_Riada" title="Liadh N\xc3\xad Riada">Liadh N\xc3\xad Riada</a> was elected in the <a href="/wiki/South_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South (European Parliament constituency)">South</a> constituency, and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Carthy" title="Matt Carthy">Matt Carthy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midlands%E2%80%93North-West_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Midlands\xe2\x80\x93North-West (European Parliament constituency)">Midlands\xe2\x80\x93North-West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Nordsieck-1"><span
